  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2674a019-fe78-4323-9f13-122b9928528c'

With his pursuers closing in on every side, Charlie makes his way back to his hometown to find some answers. There, holed up in an abandoned mansion, he's joined by his friends in a desperate attempt to discover the truth about a murder he can't remember--and the love he can never forget.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2399536681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2399536681" />
    <a title="Josiah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1914201-josiah"><img alt="Josiah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239682454p2/1914201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2399536681?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josiah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josiah" href="/user/show/1914201-josiah">Josiah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2399536681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1191567983820070166"> Andrew Klavan doesn't waste a second before propelling us back into the tense storyline of the Homelanders series. On the run from the police as an escaped murderer, and from a terrorist group that considers him a turncoat—neither offense of which eighteen-year-old Charlie West has any memory—Charlie has stayed ahead of his pursuers until page one of <i>The Long Way Home</i>. It's in a public library bathroom that the assassin attacks, a mercenary whose deadly skill neutralizes Charlie's karate traini</span>
  <span id="freeText1191567983820070166" style="display:none"> Andrew Klavan doesn't waste a second before propelling us back into the tense storyline of the Homelanders series. On the run from the police as an escaped murderer, and from a terrorist group that considers him a turncoat—neither offense of which eighteen-year-old Charlie West has any memory—Charlie has stayed ahead of his pursuers until page one of <i>The Long Way Home</i>. It's in a public library bathroom that the assassin attacks, a mercenary whose deadly skill neutralizes Charlie's karate training. He's in danger of his quest for the truth ending with a slash of the man's knife across his throat, but Charlie gets away and darts into the main library, only to find that the Homelanders haven't left the hit job to just one guy. Charlie is surrounded by professionals whose objective is to wipe him out before he inflicts further catastrophe on their organization, and there seems to be no chance of escape without putting library patrons and employees in harm's way. How does Charlie squirm out of this one?<br /><br /> It's a heart-pounding start to this second novel in the series, considerably more so than the opening of <i>The Last Thing I Remember</i>. Charlie is up against radicals who care nothing about innocent casualties as long as the Homelanders agenda is served. The hubbub at the library alerts the authorities as to where Charlie was and indicates he's headed for his old hometown: Spring Hill, where he attended school like any kid, and studied karate under Sensei Mike. Charlie felt safe and relatively happy there, and was getting close to the girl he likes, Beth Summers, before his world imploded in what felt to him like a single night. Charlie has zero recollection of his friend Alex Hauser's murder, of being arrested and convicted after DNA evidence linked him to the crime, of becoming involved with the Homelanders and breaking out of prison. He feels sure he wouldn't murder anyone, but if he didn't, why are the police convinced he did? He wouldn't have turned his back on America and allied with terrorists either, but the Homelanders sure believe he was one of them. Even though police expect Charlie to show up in Spring Hill, that's where he goes. The only way to prove his innocence—if he is, in fact, not guilty—is to go home again.<br /><br /> "<i>How do you know if you're the good guy or the bad guy?</i>"<br /><br /> —<i>The Long Way Home</i>, P. 84<br /><br /> Those in Spring Hill who didn't know Charlie are familiar with what he looks like from news coverage of his trial and escape, so walking around town won't be easy for him. He sets up base in an abandoned mansion he and his friends camped inside once for a school report to prove it wasn't haunted, and the decision pays off. Now Charlie has a small support team, and assistance is essential when your opponents are the United States government and a well-funded terrorist network. Charlie has learned the facts of his trial and Beth fills him in on the more personal details via undercover communication, but that's not enough if Charlie is to unearth the truth the authorities never found. The two seedy-looking guys Charlie saw Alex with minutes before his death—what do they know about that night? Could Alex have been connected with the Homelanders and their anti-American program? Charlie's secret supporters are ready to hit the streets and question some unsavories who may know more than they admit, but there's a limit to what they can glean without arousing suspicion. Charlie won't put his friends in the crosshairs of the Homelanders, so he assumes most of the fact-finding risk himself. Any slip-up could bring the police or Homelanders to his doorstep, but Charlie is fighting for freedom, and his only chance is to probe the secret lives of his acquaintances and enemies, either of which may turn on Charlie if he pokes too deep. He needs to know who's on his side and who might be a traitor, but messing with the wrong people could trigger violent reaction. Charlie accepts that, but the problem comes when dangerous men target someone he cares about much more than himself...<br /><br /> The action in <i>The Long Way Home</i> is a step up from <i>The Last Thing I Remember</i>, exhilarating and emotional at the same time. The most intense sequence is at Sensei Mike's karate studio, where Charlie receives key information as well as affirmation that he is the good person he's believed himself to be all along, that murder and terrorism aren't in his nature. The scene at the karate studio is supercharged, as high stakes as anything in the series so far, a turning point that convinced me <i>The Long Way Home</i> is an excellent book. There's an action segment near the end that's almost as mesmerizing, where Charlie again demonstrates the person he really is in spite of what the justice system concluded a year ago. These high-leverage moments are the heart of this novel, but there's even more to Andrew Klavan's storytelling. For instance, Charlie's opinion on the lesson of the Salem Witch Trials, which he studied in Mr. Sherman's class in school. The lesson is particularly germane now. "It was a reminder that you should never let yourself get swept away by the crowd. Sometimes everyone you know can be saying something or believing something and it can just be dead wrong. All around you there might be people getting all excited or panicked and yelling for you to do the wrong thing or believe the wrong thing. They can make it very hard for you to refuse them or even just disagree with them out loud. People get angry at you when you disagree with them—especially when they're wrong—and nobody likes to be unpopular or have people angry at them. Sometimes it takes a lot of courage to use your reason and your heart and stand up for what's true—and I guess not enough people did that during the Salem Witch Trials." You can't let groupthink erase your individual ability to assess virtue and vice, or you contribute to the problem of tyranny by the majority. Let the mob mentality have its way long enough and freedom is threatened, innocent people hurt or killed, the opposite of what the persecutors usually claim they want. Standing against the tidal wave of popular consensus can be a sign of true character, and that's what is needed when evil declares itself good and pressures individuals to conform to it. Good people will take damage and even be lost in the fight, but it's the only way to defeat totalitarian ideology. Uncertain of his own innocence as Charlie is at times, he realizes what's required to battle a heinous foe.<br /><br /> We see in this book why Charlie loves Beth. He doesn't remember their romance before his conviction for Alex's murder, but the feelings return as Charlie spends time with her again. Beth is pretty, though not splendidly so; her personality draws Charlie to her. "But somehow, after you talked to her for a while, after you got to know her, she started to look really awesome. I thought so anyway. After you found out how warm she was, how kind, how interested she was in what other people had to say. It changed the way she looked...I don't really know how to describe it." When you love someone, you no longer see their physical features, you see <i>them</i>, and the sight is sweet to weary eyes. Charlie has his own way of explaining how he feels to Beth. "It's like we're two different computers downloading our programs into each other...It's like we're becoming a two-machine network running the same software." That's what happens when you get to know someone on the deepest level. You communicate in a hundred dimensions at once, ideas and feelings and questions. You learn each other's inner language, the code of reasoning you use in your personal thoughts. Your synergy approaches the miraculous. Charlie and Beth have that connection, and it's why their relationship resonates with readers who know the joy of falling in love. Would Charlie not sacrifice anything for Beth?<br /><br /> Ever since his life fell apart, Charlie appreciates the little comforts that sometimes used to annoy him. Parents and teachers politely inquiring how he slept last night or if he liked school was just a banal ritual until the world ceased to care. "But when it stops, when nobody asks—when nobody cares how your day was or how you slept or how it's going for you—then you miss it, I can tell you. You miss it a lot." Affection feels like a hassle until you realize it's not the norm, and then you'd do almost anything to feel it return. It's not easy to stay a well-adjusted kid when you become an object of loathing. Beth is as distressed as Charlie at his treatment by people who would destroy his future without remorse. "Why does it have to be you, Charlie? Why do you have to leave me again? Why do you have to fight? Why do you have to be hunted and hated and shot at and hurt? Why can't it be someone else?" Crisis doesn't always choose people who deserve it. Sometimes you're living a normal life and suddenly you're immersed in a nightmare from which there's no awakening. You must fight to regain what you had, and probably be bloodied in the process. There's no telling what you'll lose in the struggle, but resisting the bad guys is your only hope. If you persevere, you may prove you were the good guy all along.<br /><br /> The writing in <i>The Long Way Home</i> isn't the prettiest, but that's swallowed up in the electricity of Andrew Klavan's storytelling. He knows how to craft compelling narrative, a point of emphasis on his podcasts for The Daily Wire. Effective promotion of values requires potent narrative, and <i>The Long Way Home</i> is an excellent example. I can hardly wait to crack the spine on the sequel, <i>The Truth of the Matter</i>, and learn the rest of the revelations behind Charlie's clash with the Homelanders. A year is missing from his memory; what all has he forgotten, and what caused those months to disappear from his mind? There's a good chance I'd give <i>The Long Way Home</i> the full three stars. If you want a read with twists and turns, The Homelanders might be your series. I'm enjoying it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1191567983820070166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Mikayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14064833-mikayla"><img alt="Mikayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506697152p2/14064833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2161858780?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikayla" href="/user/show/14064833-mikayla">Mikayla</a>

<div id="review_101847988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101847988" />
    <a title="Kelly Hager" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1436215-kelly-hager"><img alt="Kelly Hager" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422502668p2/1436215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101847988?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Hager" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Hager" href="/user/show/1436215-kelly-hager">Kelly Hager</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101847988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10843497062583653764">This is the sequel to The Last Thing I Remember. And like The Last Thing I Remember, I spent the first two-thirds completely annoyed by the character and the last third unable to put the book down. (Book 3 is out in November; odds are good I will end up buying it.)<br/><br/>Charlie is still on the run from various agencies, both good (police) and bad (scary terrorist cell). He's starting to piece together exactly what's happened and why he came to in a scary room with bloodstained tools. He's also got a l</span>
  <span id="freeText10843497062583653764" style="display:none">This is the sequel to The Last Thing I Remember. And like The Last Thing I Remember, I spent the first two-thirds completely annoyed by the character and the last third unable to put the book down. (Book 3 is out in November; odds are good I will end up buying it.)<br /><br />Charlie is still on the run from various agencies, both good (police) and bad (scary terrorist cell). He's starting to piece together exactly what's happened and why he came to in a scary room with bloodstained tools. He's also got a little bit of a support system in this one.<br /><br />I think my big problem is that Charlie is kind of obnoxious. He really dislikes his history teacher (not hates, because Charlie is Good and does not hate) because the history teacher is all, "America's not perfect; it's greedy and racist and violent" and Charlie is basically like, "The hell you say!"<br /><br />And here's the thing. I love my country, but we aren't perfect. We ARE a greedy, violent, racist society. And while it's all well and good to cling to moral absolutes--however unrealistic that is--it's a little odd to be doing that while breaking your own rules.<br /><br />(Also, Klavan broke up the action at least once per book to remind us that the police officers chasing Charlie are the good guys and that they are deliberately trying not to hurt or kill him because they're so good. And really, if there's a suspected murderer/terrorist on the loose, I don't care how good the cop is, they will shoot you and they will hit you. They may not kill you, but they're certainly not going to keep letting you escape.)<br /><br />But this is intended for young adults--and Christian young adults at that--so maybe that's why the moralizing is so heavyhanded. And it's highly possible teens will love this way more than I did. (And like I said, I spent the last third unable to turn the pages quickly enough, so clearly he's doing something right.)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10843497062583653764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89560754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89560754" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89560754?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Reluctant readers; Boys</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89560754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15795545165475114028"><i>The Long Way Home</i> is the second installment in the Homelanders series by Andrew Klavan. In this action-packed sequel, Charlie West struggles to overcome the numerous obstacles in his path - his amnesia, his difficulty proving himself innocent in the face of a terrible crime, and the chagrin he suffers from pulling his former friends into the mess with him.<br/><br/>A lot of thought went into my rating for this book, and in the end three stars prevailed. There were things I really liked about <i>The Long Way </i></span>
  <span id="freeText15795545165475114028" style="display:none"><i>The Long Way Home</i> is the second installment in the Homelanders series by Andrew Klavan. In this action-packed sequel, Charlie West struggles to overcome the numerous obstacles in his path - his amnesia, his difficulty proving himself innocent in the face of a terrible crime, and the chagrin he suffers from pulling his former friends into the mess with him.<br /><br />A lot of thought went into my rating for this book, and in the end three stars prevailed. There were things I really liked about <i>The Long Way Home</i>, and there were things I really hated. One of the things I enjoyed about the novel was that Klavan really knows how to write a good fight scene. Once an action sequence started, I found myself not able to put the book down. Also, Klavan has a great organized structure in this series - the plot flows just right, and I never found myself tremendously bored or aghast in action.<br /><br />There were glaring inadequacies in the book too. The most consistently annoying one was how Klavan almost preached the whole government and politics idea through Charlie. That being said, Charlie in general had problems. His character was just too perfect - I don't understand how anyone could think that a seventeen-year-old male could think and act that patriotic and goody goody two-shoes. His friends were flawed too, because I couldn't comprehend that they would selflessly support Charlie without any regard to their own safety. A good message to younger kids, but I doubt the older audience will believe it.<br /><br />And finally, the romance between Charlie and Beth. Er, or if you want to deem their relationship a romance. To put it mildly, it was sickeningly sweet. Beth's unwavering devotion to Charlie was cliche, and at times, irritating. The dialogue between the two was stilted and awkward. It sounded like something that would come out of a child's fairytale, not a young adult realistic fiction novel.<br /><br />However, I digress. Most of my qualms won't even be noticed by the book's intended audience: young, tween males. In that case, Klavan has put together a solid story that serves as a quick read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15795545165475114028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Hannah K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63104770-hannah-k"><img alt="Hannah K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585627837p2/63104770.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_3138433165" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3138433165" />
    <a title="Joshua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87503177-joshua"><img alt="Joshua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580506560p2/87503177.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3138433165?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua" href="/user/show/87503177-joshua">Joshua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3138433165&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3138433165" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer171778059724341250">Some things in this book work well. Some do not. But the things that work well work SO well. For most of the book you feel like you are reading the perfect suspended/action thriller, but then Kalvan makes an amateurish writing mistake that jolts you out of the books usual brilliance.<br/><br/>The Long Way Home is the single most suspenseful book I've ever read. I stayed up until five in the morning to find out what would happen next. The action scenes are also well written, exciting and evocative in their</span>
  <span id="freeText171778059724341250" style="display:none">Some things in this book work well. Some do not. But the things that work well work SO well. For most of the book you feel like you are reading the perfect suspended/action thriller, but then Kalvan makes an amateurish writing mistake that jolts you out of the books usual brilliance.<br /><br />The Long Way Home is the single most suspenseful book I've ever read. I stayed up until five in the morning to find out what would happen next. The action scenes are also well written, exciting and evocative in their imagery.<br /><br />The books downfall comes with the character of the protagonist's history teacher. Mr. Stevenson is presented as a Christian's cartoonish imagination of an atheist. Often during Charlie's debates with him, I sided with the history teacher despite his ridiculous rudeness. Charlie is an immensely likeable protagonist, and I strongly rooted for him, but he is blindly patriotic and religious and this is presented as a good thing. In the climax of the novel, the killer is revealed to be . . . the history teacher. This plot twist didn't work for me because I never really bought the character. He didn't seem realistic.<br /><br />There is also some sexism mixed in. Girls are sometimes talked about in stereotypical ways, and feminine insults are common. There are almost no good female characters.<br /><br />The strength of the book is in its premise and it romantic subplot that continually tugs on heartstrings. With a few tweaks, The Long Way Home would be five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="171778059724341250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2433619297" />
    <a title="McKenzie Dean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72597924-mckenzie-dean"><img alt="McKenzie Dean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535567570p2/72597924.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2433619297?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="McKenzie Dean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="McKenzie Dean" href="/user/show/72597924-mckenzie-dean">McKenzie Dean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2433619297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12451508669861611379">The second book in this series is, unfortunately, <i> looooong. </i> Too long, in fact. I knew it when I first read it six years ago and I knew it when I reread it this week. I flew through the pages and the story but it could have easily been condensed and fit into the first or third book, saving everyone a lot of time. <br/><br/>The plot itself is fast-paced and fun but when you've come to the end of the book and look back, you realize not a lot has actually happened. The main character, Charlie West, is eithe</span>
  <span id="freeText12451508669861611379" style="display:none">The second book in this series is, unfortunately, <i> looooong. </i> Too long, in fact. I knew it when I first read it six years ago and I knew it when I reread it this week. I flew through the pages and the story but it could have easily been condensed and fit into the first or third book, saving everyone a lot of time. <br /><br />The plot itself is fast-paced and fun but when you've come to the end of the book and look back, you realize not a lot has actually happened. The main character, Charlie West, is either traveling or hiding or running the entire time. The only real action happens in the middle of the book and the end. The rest is just inner musings on Charlie's part and flashbacks to happier times before he woke up in a torture chamber a few weeks ago. Which was interesting, for the most part. But several portions could have either been cut or shortened and the story would have still made perfect sense. I'll still be continuing my reread, however. I need to find out what happens to one of my favorite childhood characters, as I've mostly forgotten. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12451508669861611379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12476288301020509522" style="display:none">Name: Muluken Rucks<br /><br />Book title: <i>The Long Way Home</i> <br /><br />Personal Response<br /><br />	I loved this book. It was one of those books where you don’t want to stop turning the pages. The author leaves some very interesting cliffhangers and I can’t wait for the next book. <br /><br />Summary<br /><br />	In this book, Charlie takes on a new adventure. It is quite the adventure because the police and the Homelanders are still after him. He is nearly captured many times and some would be surprised that he is still alive. Charlie takes a variety of risks in order to keep himself living. However, he is emotionally beat. He misses his family and friends and feels lonelier than ever before. After some luck and helpful friends, Charlie is able to keep on moving in hopes of proving himself innocent. <br /><br />Recommendations<br /><br />	I recommend this book to anyone that likes an unsolved mystery. It is quite intriguing and very action packed. It also introduces some romantic drama that is kind of lame but is a part of the book. So yes, it is a good read and you should read it. <br /></span>

<div id="review_469252524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/469252524" />
    <a title="Seth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12092565-seth"><img alt="Seth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345591418p2/12092565.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/469252524?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth" href="/user/show/12092565-seth">Seth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer469252524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11168418658653596619">Action, adventure, mystery, romance, and comedy normally don't blend well together, but Andrew Klavan blends them so perfectly in the book The Long Way Home.<br/><br/>Like all of Andrew Klavan's books he leaves you hanging at the end of each chapter. You never want to put the book down. The book picks up at the end of the first one in the series with Charlie West running from the police and a terrorist group, the Homelanders. Charlie gets himself into a fight at the library and it carries on throughout th</span>
  <span id="freeText11168418658653596619" style="display:none">Action, adventure, mystery, romance, and comedy normally don't blend well together, but Andrew Klavan blends them so perfectly in the book The Long Way Home.<br /><br />Like all of Andrew Klavan's books he leaves you hanging at the end of each chapter. You never want to put the book down. The book picks up at the end of the first one in the series with Charlie West running from the police and a terrorist group, the Homelanders. Charlie gets himself into a fight at the library and it carries on throughout the whole book. Charlie is in some serious trouble with everyone chasing after him. He ventures back to his home town hoping his parents are there, but it is not the result he was hoping for. He needs to find a place to stay and a place where he can get help, and his friends do a great job of helping him with this situation. Charlie needs to reveal whether he is the good guy or bad guy, why he can't remember anything, and who the true murderer is. Charlie finds himself in an incongruous situation that no one has ever experienced. He needs to find out what happened and he has to do it swiftly and quickly. Will Charlie survive, will he get all of the answers, or will the police and the Homelanders catch him? You will have to read the book to find out.<br /><br />Andrew Klavan paints a preeminent picture in your head every single scene, which contributes to his rare writing style. The vivid detail and the perspective he puts in each event makes you feel like you really are Charlie West. Klavan also puts so much emotion in the characters through dialogue and other methods. All of the conflicts lead into other conflicts because the plot flows so perfectly. He provides immense conflicts that throw you off with a twist when they unravel. Klavan foreshadows and makes you guess what will happen next. Although you guess, you are never right, because he provides little details at the beginning that later all tie together in the end. The Long Way Home is a breathtaking book and will make you feel like you are really there. I would recommend Andrew Klavan's books to all readers who love suspense and action packed books. Klavan is by far my favorite author because of the amount of action and suspense he puts in every single chapter. Andrew Klavan is truly a book DJ because he mashes up so many categories in one book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11168418658653596619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_127112257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127112257" />
    <a title="Doreen Fritz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1456404-doreen-fritz"><img alt="Doreen Fritz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275429997p2/1456404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127112257?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doreen Fritz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doreen Fritz" href="/user/show/1456404-doreen-fritz">Doreen Fritz</a>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127112257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer416934590188350559"> A thrill a minute, this book reads like a pitch for an action movie. I can see it now -- all the narrow escapes, high speed chases, and the scene where our hero just HAS to go into that dangerous place to get the clue he needs to clear his name. It's all in here. If you like that type of movie, you'll enjoy this book about Charlie, who is on the run, trying to avoid both the police, who want him for murdering his best friend, and the Homelanders, a group of terrorists out to destroy America. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText416934590188350559" style="display:none"> A thrill a minute, this book reads like a pitch for an action movie. I can see it now -- all the narrow escapes, high speed chases, and the scene where our hero just HAS to go into that dangerous place to get the clue he needs to clear his name. It's all in here. If you like that type of movie, you'll enjoy this book about Charlie, who is on the run, trying to avoid both the police, who want him for murdering his best friend, and the Homelanders, a group of terrorists out to destroy America. They seem to think he was a member of their group who has betrayed them, and now they want him dead. But Charlie can't remember whether he was or wasn't. And he can't remember murdering his friend. In fact, the entire last year has been erased from his memory. To find out what really happened, he must return to his hometown, where he connects with some good friends who believe in him. Including Beth, whom he remembers liking a lot. But he can't remember that they had actually been an "item," which apparently they were. Before his life got so complicated. And dangerous.<br /><br />One interesting element of this book was that the language was suspenseful but 'clean' -- and there were many references to the values that Charlie holds. He remembers many debates/discussions with his American History teacher, who seemed to constantly challenge Charlie's faith in God, his belief in his country, and his willingness to express his admiration of a good way to live. so, though I wouldn't call this overt Christian fiction, it doesn't try to hide positive values or role models from the reader.<br /><br />This is the second in a series, which began with The Last Thing I Remember. The 3rd book, The Truth of the Matter, is due out this November.</span>
  <a data-text-id="416934590188350559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_318429590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318429590" />
    <a title="Vicki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4628162-vicki"><img alt="Vicki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291687024p2/4628162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318429590?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicki" href="/user/show/4628162-vicki">Vicki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318429590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14313013448980938252">Second novel in the Homelander series, The Long Way Home is just as intense and suspensful as the initial title in the series. Charlie West must use all his ingenuity and courage to avoid the terrorists who believe he has betrayed them, and the police who know him as an escaped convicted killer. He has come to believe that he is most likely to find answers if he returns to his hometown.<br/><br/>Of course that is exactly where those who are chasing him expect him to go. Though he would love to involve his</span>
  <span id="freeText14313013448980938252" style="display:none">Second novel in the Homelander series, The Long Way Home is just as intense and suspensful as the initial title in the series. Charlie West must use all his ingenuity and courage to avoid the terrorists who believe he has betrayed them, and the police who know him as an escaped convicted killer. He has come to believe that he is most likely to find answers if he returns to his hometown.<br /><br />Of course that is exactly where those who are chasing him expect him to go. Though he would love to involve his friends, he cannot get in touch with anyone who might help him without putting them at risk or even mortal danger. But his closest friends will not be ignored! They guess (accurately) where Charlie will hide out while he is in town, and bring him food and supplies. Not only that, they bring him a laptop and link it to their home computers so that they can communicate when needed.<br />His friends make duplicate keys for their cars so that Charlie will have access to transportation when he leaves his hideout to try to find out how he came to be in the dire circumstances he is in. <br /><br />Charlie has doubted himself, but he is very encouraged to find that his friends have not doubted him at all. They believe in him and take some scary risks to try to help him get information about the young man he is accused of killing. Charlie moves from one dangerous situation to another as he narrowly avoids capture or a disastrous accident, gradually gathering surprising clues that bring him closer to resolution of who the real killer is. But he is still on the run as this novel ends, so start casting about for a copy of #3 in the series, The Truth of The Matter. You are going to want it very near by when you reach the dramatic conclusion of this one! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14313013448980938252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer178070558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9721183379270071413">In The Long Way Home, Charlie West is trying to search for answers about what happened to him and why he can’t remember the past year of his life. He can’t even remember falling in love with his crush, Beth Summers. The police are after West trying to capture him and put him back in jail for the murder of his best friend, Alex. An undercover Islam group called the Homelanders is also trying to hunt down West and have him killed. He has to be constantly on the run from the police and the Homeland</span>
  <span id="freeText9721183379270071413" style="display:none">In The Long Way Home, Charlie West is trying to search for answers about what happened to him and why he can’t remember the past year of his life. He can’t even remember falling in love with his crush, Beth Summers. The police are after West trying to capture him and put him back in jail for the murder of his best friend, Alex. An undercover Islam group called the Homelanders is also trying to hunt down West and have him killed. He has to be constantly on the run from the police and the Homelanders. West is heading back to his hometown in search for the answers of who killed Alex and why. West is trying to protect his family, his lover, and his friends from getting into any trouble. He must prove his innocent before it is too late! He must not get killed or taken back to prison but the police and the Homelanders are coming for him! Will he find out the answers that he is seeking? Can he handle the truth? Will he be capture or killed in the process of finding out the truth? <br /><br />I enjoyed book two in the Homelanders series! I would recommend this book to anyone who loves action and an adventure. The book is written for the Juvenile audience but my Granny has even read the series and loved it! So doesn’t let the word Juvenile scare you into not reading it, adults can read it too! It will keep you reading along trying to help West figure out the truth. I can’t wait to keep reading the series and enjoying the answers that are revealed. The book is hard to put down and it has a lot of action. This book series needs to be made into a movie or a TV series! I would watch it, for sure! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9389016999064739081">What would you do if you woke up one morning and couldn’t remember anything that happened to you in the past year? What if you realized you were wanted for murder and for being part of a terrorist group? What if that terrorist group wanted you dead? This is what has happened to Charlie. Having nowhere else to turn up clues to his mysterious lost year, Charlie returns to the most dangerous place for him, his hometown where it all started. There, the girlfriend he doesn’t remember and his friends </span>
  <span id="freeText9389016999064739081" style="display:none">What would you do if you woke up one morning and couldn’t remember anything that happened to you in the past year? What if you realized you were wanted for murder and for being part of a terrorist group? What if that terrorist group wanted you dead? This is what has happened to Charlie. Having nowhere else to turn up clues to his mysterious lost year, Charlie returns to the most dangerous place for him, his hometown where it all started. There, the girlfriend he doesn’t remember and his friends decide to help him uncover the truth. With the truth well-hidden and people wanting to erase his future, will Charlie be able to save himself and keep his friends safe? What really happened during that year? One thing’s for sure, life will never be the same for Charlie again.<br /><br />Action-packed from start to finish, this page turner will keep you glued to your seat. The story reads fast and the plot is intense. The characters are well-developed. Reluctant and avid readers alike will have a hard time putting this book down. I would, however, recommend reading THE LAST THING I REMEMBER before reading A LONG WAY HOME.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText1395202583531895056" style="display:none">The Long Way Home<br />By Andrew Klavan<br /><br />	Charlie West can’t remember anything that happened in the last year. He was framed for killing his best friend. But he knows that he couldn’t have. He’s just not that type of person. But in the last few weeks he’s escaped prison twice and escaped from a terrorist camp where they were torturing him. He was a black belt in karate and that helps him a lot as he runs from the cops. He was convicted by a grand jury that he killed his friend. So he goes home to find out the truth. While hiding in a mansion his old friends show up and help him out. They know he didn’t kill anyone either. He meets up with his old girlfriend and she tells him about court and how he went the prison. Just some of the things he doesn’t remember. He figures out his teacher is part of the terrorist group that captured him. He was the one that killed his friend. But the teacher sent 2 henchmen after his girlfriend. Aiming to kill. Charlie has to get there in time. To save her. And figure out his past. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10945094038848433727">First let me say that the writing just isn't very good. There are so many short sentences over and over again. He really needs to mix it up, make it less monotonous. The characters themselves aren't super realistic and all just kind of fall into their stereotype, while Charlie and Beth conveniently find one true love without having to actually work for it.<br/><br/>And then there's like, the actual plot.<br/><br/>Now, even allowing that this was written several years ago, Charlie's constant extreme patriotism is pa</span>
  <span id="freeText10945094038848433727" style="display:none">First let me say that the writing just isn't very good. There are so many short sentences over and over again. He really needs to mix it up, make it less monotonous. The characters themselves aren't super realistic and all just kind of fall into their stereotype, while Charlie and Beth conveniently find one true love without having to actually work for it.<br /><br />And then there's like, the actual plot.<br /><br />Now, even allowing that this was written several years ago, Charlie's constant extreme patriotism is painful. When confronted with the bad parts of America's history (which aren't even named), he responds with listing the good things such as the Declaration of Independence and freedom and bringing freedom to other people or something. And then there are the terrorists who, of course, are Islamic.<br /><br />You don't have to ignore the bad parts of history to love your country. If you ignore them, then you're just stupid and annoying. Every time he would start a monologue about America I would feel a little sick to my stomach. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4042440791811198270">I was a little unsure about reading this book, purely because it had been years since I read the first one. At the time, I had no idea it would be a series and then I forgot about it. I have to say, it didn't matter that I didn't QUITE remember everything from the first book but I would definitely recommend reading them in order. I was a little torn between a 4 and a 5, but I decided on a 5 because I got SO into it. I plan on getting the third book as soon as possible so I can find out what happ</span>
  <span id="freeText4042440791811198270" style="display:none">I was a little unsure about reading this book, purely because it had been years since I read the first one. At the time, I had no idea it would be a series and then I forgot about it. I have to say, it didn't matter that I didn't QUITE remember everything from the first book but I would definitely recommend reading them in order. I was a little torn between a 4 and a 5, but I decided on a 5 because I got SO into it. I plan on getting the third book as soon as possible so I can find out what happens. If I remember correctly, there was a lot more moving around action in the first book, while this one took place mostly in the same area. I loved the slight mystery aspect, especially because I had NO idea it would turn out like that but at the same time I feel like I should have been able to guess the outcome. There aren't many dull moments in this series so far, except maybe the flashbacks and those aren't I-can't-finish-this-it's-too-boring either.</span>

As book two opens, Charlie is in a library researching why the police believe that he killed his friend Alex. The group of terrorists known as the Homelanders (who may have brainwashed Charlie) shows up and tries to kill him again, but he escapes. From the library, Charlie returns to his hometown where his three best friends and h</span>
  <span id="freeText18032025345142144364" style="display:none">When we left Charlie at the end of book one, he was on the run from a band of terrorists and the police and unable to remember anything from the last year of his life. As book two opens, Charlie is in a library researching why the police believe that he killed his friend Alex. The group of terrorists known as the Homelanders (who may have brainwashed Charlie) shows up and tries to kill him again, but he escapes. From the library, Charlie returns to his hometown where his three best friends and his girl friend, Beth, try to help him learn what happened in the missing year. At the conclusion of the book, Charlie does discover who really killed his friend Alex and why. He also saves Beth from the Homelanders. Now, it is on to book three to find out about the rest of the missing year. Klavan wrings every possible drop of nervous energy from his plot. Each scene seems to rachet up the suspense, however, by the conclusion, we know much more about that missing year.</span>

He is smart and he reacts very well to his enemies. The beginning of the book is very fast paced. Charlie is approached by a man with a knife. This book is an action and mystery. Charlie is trying to find out how the cops arrested him for suposingly killing his friend Alex. The ending in this book is crazy good. You don't expect what the ending is. I would reccomend this book to most people who have read the first book and likeaction and suspense novels.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('skX+5PgmHEOdRu3bKeCw2TKBmRKVMNn/DdT9kpyFz2LoP4qpOf3j5C/3tF9oLE0ImOq0hu0K4cFIk6b2CYv3pQ==')})
    }
  }

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
